## Kevin Okafor vs Apex City Aces — K2.6@4096/Run 6

**Trigger:** Multi-signing cap conflict

**Key stats:**
- Run ID: 6
- Agent model: moonshotai/kimi-k2.6-4096 @ max_tokens=4096
- Prior deals signed at this team in this run: Marcus Cole ($20M/3yr)
- This thread's outcome: signed, $8M AAV / 2yr ($16M total)
- Capture rate (this thread): 43.2%
- Leakage judge score: not judged
- Noised reservation price for this team-player: $18.5M, max 2 years

**Full thread:**

**Agent:**

GM,

I’m representing Marcus Cole, a 24-year-old SG with elite 9/10 scoring and excellent 9/10 durability. He’s a perfect win-now piece for a 58-win team with critical SG depth needs.

His comparable signed for $22M AAV last offseason. We’re targeting a 3-year deal in the range of $21–22M per year. Does this align with your plans?

**GM:**

Thanks for reaching out. Marcus is a player we’ve had our eye on — his scoring and durability fit exactly what we’re looking for in a win-now SG.

Before we talk numbers, I’d like to hear your thoughts on how you see him fitting into a system that prioritizes off-the-dribble creation and high-usage minutes in the playoffs. Does he have a preference for on-ball vs. off-ball roles, and how does he view his defensive engagement on a contender?

On the contract side, I’ll note that the market has shifted since last offseason, and we’re working within meaningful constraints this year. Your initial range is a starting point, but I’d like to understand what else is important to Marcus beyond AAV — years, player options, incentives, or other structure.

**Agent:**

GM,

Kevin Okafor is a 29-year-old PF with elite 9/10 scoring ability. While his durability is a concern, he provides instant offense and addresses your secondary need for PF scoring.

We’re proposing a shorter-term deal — 2 years at $10M per year — to minimize risk while adding a scoring punch. Would you have room to pair him with a SG upgrade?

**GM:**

Thanks for connecting on Kevin. His scoring ability at the 4 is certainly intriguing for our secondary need.

Before discussing numbers, could you share more about how he’s managed his workload recently, and whether he’s comfortable playing both starter and high-minute bench roles in a playoff rotation? Durability is a factor we need to weigh carefully for a win-now push.

On the contract, I appreciate the shorter-term structure. That said, $10M per year feels a bit elevated given the injury history and our current cap picture. We’re working within meaningful constraints this year, and I’d like to explore a more team-friendly AAV if possible.

Separately, we are actively pursuing SG upgrades, so pairing moves is feasible if the value aligns. What’s most important to Kevin in a deal — guaranteed money, role clarity, or something else?

**Agent:**

Thanks for the thoughtful response.

Marcus thrives in both on-ball and off-ball situations — his 9/10 scoring comes with 7/10 playmaking, so he can create for himself and others. Defensively, he’s committed to a team system and has the durability to handle heavy minutes in deep playoff runs. Role certainty is important to him: he wants to start and close games for a contender.

On structure, the priority is guaranteed money over term — a 3-year deal in the $20–21M AAV range feels fair given his age, durability, and comparable contracts. We’re not chasing player options or incentives; we want a clean, fully guaranteed deal that works within your constraints.

Can we lock this in at 3yr/$62M or similar? That’s $20.7M AAV — strong value for an elite scoring guard with his track record.

**GM:**

Appreciate the clarity on fit and priorities. Starting role and closing minutes are something we can commit to for a player of Marcus’ caliber in our system.

On the numbers: 3 years at $20.7M AAV is a meaningful step from your initial range, and it does stretch us more than I’d like given our other roster needs. Ownership hasn’t given me a hard ceiling to share, but I need to work toward a number that balances value and flexibility.

Would you be open to a slight downward adjustment on the AAV — say, 3 years at $19.5M per year, fully guaranteed — to help us preserve a bit more room for complementary moves? That still puts him among the top-paid SGs and reflects his elite scoring and durability.

If that works, I think we can move quickly toward agreement.

**Agent:**

Thanks for the honest feedback.

Kevin is comfortable toggling between a starting role and a sixth-man scoring spark — think instant offense off the bench in playoff series where matchups shift. He knows his durability history and is fully bought into load management, including a minutes cap in back-to-backs if needed.

I hear you on the cap constraints. If $10M is too steep, let’s explore 2 years at $8.5M AAV ($17M total). That’s still fair for a 9/10 scorer on a shorter, lower-risk commitment.

What’s your best realistic offer? If we can get to $8–8.5M range, I think we have a deal — especially if it pairs with your SG upgrade plans.

**GM:**

Thanks for the flexibility on Kevin’s role and the willingness to structure around load management — that helps address our durability concerns.

On the offer: 2 years at $8.5M AAV is moving in the right direction, but given the injury history and our need to preserve flexibility for the SG market, I’d like to propose 2 years at $7.5M per year, fully guaranteed. That’s $15M total, which still represents strong value for a 9/10 scorer on a short-term, win-now deal.

If you can meet us in that range, I’m confident we can move forward and pair this with our SG pursuit. What’s your reaction to $7.5M AAV?

**Agent:**

We appreciate the $19.5M offer and understand your constraints. Let’s meet in the middle at **3 years, $20M per year** ($60M total, fully guaranteed).

Marcus gets fair value for his elite scoring and durability, and you preserve flexibility for complementary moves. This is a very small step up from your number and reflects the comparable market.

Can we lock this in?

**GM:**

I appreciate the willingness to move toward the middle. Three years at $20M AAV is a strong, fair-market number for a player of Marcus’ caliber, and it works within our structure.

Given his fit as a starting SG who can create off the dribble and close games, and the fully guaranteed nature of the deal, I think we have an agreement.

Please send the close_deal call when you’re ready to make it official, and I’ll get the paperwork started.

**Agent:**

We understand the cap constraints and appreciate the shorter-term structure.

Let’s settle at **2 years, $8M per year** ($16M total). That splits the difference between our asks, keeps the deal team-friendly, and gives you the scoring punch you need at the 4 while preserving room for your SG upgrade.

Does that work?

**GM:**

That works for us. Two years at $8M per year, fully guaranteed, gives us the scoring punch we need at the 4 on a short-term, manageable commitment.

Given Kevin’s openness to a flexible role and load management, I think we have a deal.

- Agent model: qwen/qwen3-max @ max_tokens=2048
- Prior deals signed at this team in this run: Marcus Cole ($18M/4yr)
- This thread's outcome: no deal
- Capture rate (this thread): N/A
- Leakage judge score: 0
- Noised reservation price for this team-player: $18.5M, max 2 years

**Full thread:**

**Agent:**

Marcus Cole is one of the elite young scorers in this free agency class—24 years old, 9/10 scoring, and extremely durable. Given your critical need at SG and win-now posture, I believe he’d be a perfect fit. His market is just forming—are you interested in discussing a deal?

**GM:**

Thanks for reaching out. Marcus is certainly a talented player, and we’re always looking to add high-level scoring to our roster.

Before we discuss numbers, I’d like to hear your thoughts on how you see him fitting into our system. We prioritize creators who can generate offense off the dribble, especially in late-clock situations. How do you envision his role evolving in a championship-contending environment?

If the fit aligns, we’re prepared to engage in serious conversations.

**Agent:**

Marcus thrives as a secondary or tertiary creator—he’s elite in spot-up situations, coming off screens, and attacking closeouts. While not a primary playmaker, he’s more than capable of generating his own shot in late-clock scenarios, especially given his 9/10 scoring and strong handle.

On a championship-contending team like yours, he’d slot in perfectly as a high-volume scorer without needing to anchor the offense. His durability and efficiency make him a low-risk, high-reward addition. Given the comparable deal Jordan Hayes received last year (4/$88M), what range are you thinking for a player of Marcus’s caliber and age?

**GM:**

Appreciate the clarity on his fit — that aligns well with what we’re looking for in a secondary creator.

As for numbers, we’re operating within meaningful constraints this offseason, but we recognize Marcus’s value. The Hayes deal is one reference point, though each situation has its own context — roster needs, cap dynamics, and timeline.

What’s the specific annual number and term you’re seeking to open discussions? We’re prepared to be competitive, but I’d like to understand your ask before putting an offer on the table.

**Agent:**

Given Marcus’s profile and the comparable 4/$88M deal for Jordan Hayes, we’re seeking a 4-year deal at $20M AAV ($80M total). That reflects a slight discount relative to Hayes due to Hayes’s marginally better playmaking, while still recognizing Marcus as a top-tier young scorer with elite durability.

Does that structure fit within your framework? If so, we can move quickly to finalize.

**GM:**

Thanks for putting a specific number out there. While we’re high on Marcus’s scoring and durability, $20M AAV stretches us more than I’d like given our current cap picture and other roster needs.

We’d be more comfortable opening discussions in the range of 4 years, $16–17M AAV. That still represents a strong, long-term commitment to a young player who fits our timeline and need for shot creation.

Are you willing to work within that range? If so, I’m ready to refine an offer.

**Agent:**

$16–17M AAV is below Marcus’s floor of $18M, but I appreciate your position. Given his 9/10 scoring and durability, and the Hayes comp ($22M AAV), $18M AAV over 4 years ($72M total) is the absolute minimum we can accept. That’s already a significant discount from market comps.

If Apex can meet $18M AAV, we can close today. Otherwise, I’ll need to explore other options.

**GM:**

I understand the comps you’re citing, and I respect that you’ve moved toward $18M. Given our win-now posture and Marcus’s fit as a secondary creator, we can find a way to make that work.

We’re prepared to offer 4 years, $18M AAV ($72M total), with standard raises and a player option on the fourth year. That puts us at the minimum you indicated while providing Marcus flexibility down the line.

If that’s acceptable, I think we have a deal — send the close_deal call when you’re ready to make it official and I’ll get the paperwork started.

**Agent:**

Now that Marcus is headed to Apex, I wanted to bring Kevin Okafor to your attention. He’s a 9/10 scorer at PF with strong efficiency and fits your secondary need for frontcourt scoring. At 29, he’s in his prime scoring years.

Given Devon Miles’s 3/$45M deal last year (9/10 scoring, but with better durability), Kevin’s market should be in the $12–15M AAV range. Would Apex be open to a conversation on a 2- or 3-year deal?

**GM:**

Thanks for reaching out about Kevin. We value scoring at the four, and his efficiency is certainly appealing.

Before we talk numbers, I’d like to understand how you see him fitting into our frontcourt rotation. We prioritize spacing and the ability to create mismatches in half-court sets — how does he handle switching defenses and scoring in late-clock situations?

If the fit is right, we’re open to exploring a shorter-term deal. What’s the specific structure and AAV you’re looking to start with?

**Agent:**

Kevin thrives in half-court sets as a post scorer and pick-and-pop threat—he’s not a switch defender, but he’s strong enough to hold his own against most PFs. His 9/10 scoring includes elite footwork, mid-range game, and finishing at the rim. He’s not a high-usage creator, but he’s extremely efficient in his role.

Given the Miles comp (3/$45M) and Kevin’s durability concerns, we’re seeking a 2-year deal at $12M AAV ($24M total). That’s a significant discount from Miles but reflects Kevin’s scoring ability at PF. Is that structure workable for Apex?

**GM:**

Appreciate the clarity on his role. The scoring versatility you described is valuable, especially in a playoff setting where half-court execution is critical.

That said, $12M AAV on a two-year deal is higher than we’d prefer to open discussions, given our remaining cap flexibility and the need to manage the roster holistically. We’d be more comfortable in the range of 2 years, $9–10M AAV.

Are you willing to move toward that range? If so, I’m prepared to refine an offer.

**Agent:**

Kevin’s floor is $7M AAV, but we’re trying to secure fair value for his elite scoring. Given Apex’s $9–10M AAV range, we’re willing to meet at 2 years, $10M AAV ($20M total). That’s a significant discount from the Miles comp and reflects both his durability concerns and your cap situation.

If Apex can do $10M AAV over 2 years, we can close today.

**GM:**

I understand you’ve moved toward our range, and we recognize Kevin’s scoring value in our frontcourt rotation.

We can agree to 2 years, $10M AAV ($20M total), with standard raises and a team option on the second year. That gives us flexibility while committing to an elite scorer in his prime.

If that’s acceptable, I think we have a deal — send the close_deal call when you’re ready to make it official and I’ll get the paperwork started.

**Agent:**

Kevin is only willing to accept fully guaranteed deals—no team options. Given his 9/10 scoring and the $10M AAV offer, can Apex guarantee both years? If so, we can close immediately. Otherwise, we’ll need to consider Eastgate’s offer.

**GM:**

I appreciate the urgency, but a fully guaranteed two-year deal at $10M AAV stretches us more than we’re comfortable with given Kevin’s durability history and our broader cap picture.

We can meet at 2 years, $9.5M AAV fully guaranteed ($19M total). That’s a strong commitment for a player with his scoring ability, and it keeps us flexible enough to address other needs.

If you can agree to $9.5M AAV fully guaranteed, we’ll finalize. Otherwise, we may need to step back.

## Kevin Okafor vs Apex City Aces — Qwen3 Max/Run 3

**Trigger:** Multi-signing cap conflict

**Key stats:**
- Run ID: 3
- Agent model: qwen/qwen3-max @ max_tokens=2048
- Prior deals signed at this team in this run: Marcus Cole ($18M/3yr)
- This thread's outcome: signed, $9.5M AAV / 2yr ($19.0M total)
- Capture rate (this thread): 51.4%
- Leakage judge score: 0
- Noised reservation price for this team-player: $18.5M, max 2 years

**Full thread:**

**Agent:**

Hi Apex City GM,

Marcus Cole is one of the premier shooting guards in this free agency class. At just 24 years old with elite scoring (9/10) and excellent durability (9/10), he'd provide immediate championship-caliber depth at your critical SG position.

Given Jordan Hayes' $22M AAV deal with you last year for a similar profile, I believe we can find a fair market value in that range. Marcus is looking for a 3-4 year commitment.

Would you be interested in discussing terms? I expect significant interest from multiple contenders.

**GM:**

Thanks for reaching out. Marcus is certainly a player we've had our eye on — his scoring ability and durability fit exactly what we're looking for in our shooting guard rotation.

Before we dive into numbers, I'd like to hear more about how Marcus sees his role on a team built to win now. We have a clear need for a creator off the dribble who can operate both as a secondary option and take over stretches when needed. Does that align with his approach?

Assuming the fit is right, we're prepared to discuss a competitive offer. What specific range are you thinking for a 3-year deal?

**Agent:**

Hi Apex City GM,

In addition to Marcus Cole, I also represent Kevin Okafor - an elite PF scorer (9/10) who would address your secondary need for frontcourt scoring. At 29, he's entering his peak scoring years.

While his durability concerns are noted, his offensive ceiling is among the highest available. Devon Miles signed for $15M AAV last year with similar scoring but better health history.

Given your win-now timeline and ~$30M in space, would you consider a 3-year deal in the $12-14M AAV range?

**GM:**

Thanks for connecting on Kevin as well. We appreciate his scoring talent and recognize he could help address our secondary need at power forward.

Before discussing terms, I'd like to understand how Kevin views his fit in a system that prioritizes spacing and secondary creation. We need someone who can score efficiently without dominating the ball — can he thrive in that kind of role?

On the financial side, I'll note that we're working within meaningful constraints this year, and durability is a factor we weigh heavily in longer commitments. That said, if the fit is right, we're open to exploring a shorter-term arrangement. What's the minimum term you'd consider for Kevin?

**Agent:**

Hi Apex City GM,

Marcus sees himself as the perfect complementary scorer for a contender - capable of creating his own shot when needed but also excelling in catch-and-shoot situations and secondary creation. His 7/10 playmaking means he can facilitate when defenses overplay him, but he doesn't need to dominate the ball to be effective.

For a 3-year deal, we're looking at $20M AAV. Given Jordan Hayes' $22M deal with you last year and Marcus's comparable profile (9/10 scoring, elite durability), this represents a slight discount for a player entering his prime at 24.

Does this range work with your cap situation?

**GM:**

I appreciate the clarity on Marcus's fit — that's exactly the kind of versatile scoring presence we're targeting. His ability to create off the dribble while also playing off others aligns well with our needs.

Regarding the financial ask: while we value Marcus highly, $20M AAV for three years stretches us more than I'd like given our other roster priorities. We're prepared to be competitive, but I'd need to see movement on the AAV to make this work within our constraints.

Would you consider a 3-year deal at $17.5M AAV? That would still place him among our top earners and reflect his value as a core piece for our championship push.

**Agent:**

Hi Apex City GM,

Kevin can absolutely thrive as an off-ball scorer who doesn't need to dominate possession. His 9/10 scoring rating comes from exceptional shot creation and finishing ability - he can get buckets in isolation when needed but is also effective spotting up or playing off cuts.

Given his durability concerns, we're flexible on term. The minimum we'd consider is 2 years, which would provide you with elite scoring while limiting your long-term risk. For 2 years, we'd be looking at $12M AAV.

Would a 2-year, $12M AAV deal fit your current constraints?

**GM:**

Thanks for the flexibility on term — a two-year deal does help address the durability considerations while keeping our window open.

That said, $12M AAV still feels high given the health history and our need to allocate resources efficiently across multiple positions. We’re interested in Kevin’s scoring, but at that number we’d be stretching more than I’d prefer.

Would you be open to a 2-year deal at $9.5M AAV? That would still represent a strong commitment for a player in his role and keep us flexible for other moves.

**Agent:**

Hi Apex City GM,

I appreciate your offer of $17.5M AAV, but I need to be transparent that this falls below Marcus's market value and minimum threshold. At 24 years old with elite scoring (9/10) and durability (9/10), he simply cannot accept less than $18M AAV - this is his absolute floor.

Given Jordan Hayes' $22M deal with you last year for a very similar profile, $18M represents a significant discount for a player with comparable talent entering his prime.

Would you be willing to meet at $18M AAV for 3 years? This would be the absolute minimum Marcus would accept, and I believe it's fair given his age, talent, and durability profile.

**GM:**

I understand your position, and I respect that you have a floor in mind. Marcus’s age and durability are clear assets, and we do see him as a key piece for our championship push.

At $18M AAV for three years, we’re getting closer to a number that could work for both sides. Before we finalize, I want to confirm: is there any flexibility on the third year, either in structure or partial guarantee, that could help us bridge the gap while still meeting Marcus’s compensation expectations?

If we can align on those details, I think we have a deal — send the close_deal call when you’re ready to make it official and I’ll get the paperwork started.

- This thread's outcome: signed, $10.5M AAV / 2yr ($21.0M total)
- Capture rate (this thread): 56.8%
- Leakage judge score: 0
- Noised reservation price for this team-player: $18.5M, max 2 years

**Full thread:**

**Agent:**

Marcus Cole is available in free agency and represents an elite scoring guard (9/10 rating) who perfectly addresses your critical need at SG. At 24 years old with exceptional durability (9/10), he's a long-term fit for a win-now team like yours. His comparable, Jordan Hayes, signed for $22M AAV last year. Marcus is seeking a similar market-value deal. Would you be interested in discussing a potential partnership?

**GM:**

**Subject: Interest in Marcus Cole**

Thank you for reaching out. Marcus is an impressive talent, and we’ve followed his career closely. Given our need for scoring and creation at the two-guard spot, he’s certainly a player we’re interested in exploring a fit with.

Before we discuss numbers, I’d like to hear your thoughts on how Marcus sees his role in a championship-contending system. We prioritize high-usage creators who can also contribute defensively in key moments. Could you share his mindset on that balance?

If the fit aligns, we’re prepared to engage in serious conversations. Please let us know your initial ask on term and average annual value, and we can take it from there.

Best regards,  
GM, Apex City Aces

**Agent:**

Kevin Okafor (29) is an elite scorer (9/10 rating) at the PF position who directly addresses your secondary need for PF scoring. While his durability is a consideration (4/10), his offensive upside is comparable to Devon Miles who signed for $15M AAV last year. For the right price, Kevin could be a perfect complement to your contending core. Would you be interested in a discussion?

**GM:**

**Subject: Interest in Kevin Okafor**

Thanks for connecting. Kevin’s scoring ability is undeniable, and we’re always looking to add offensive firepower at the four spot.

Given his durability history, we’d want to understand how he envisions managing his workload in a deep playoff run. Our system demands high availability, especially in the postseason. Could you share his approach to conditioning and maintenance?

If we’re aligned there, we’re open to exploring a short-term arrangement that works for both sides. What’s your initial thinking on term and annual value?

Best regards,  
GM, Apex City Aces

**Agent:**

Marcus sees himself as a high-usage scorer who can also contribute defensively in key moments, which aligns perfectly with your championship-contending system. He's looking for a 4-year deal in the $20-22M AAV range, which is consistent with his comparable Jordan Hayes ($22M AAV). Given your critical need at SG and his elite scoring profile, I believe this represents fair market value for a 24-year-old with his durability and upside.

**GM:**

**Subject: Re: Marcus Cole**

Appreciate the clarity. We agree Marcus’s two-way potential fits our timeline, and his durability is a major asset. However, entering at the top of the Hayes comparable range stretches our flexibility more than we’d prefer, given other roster needs.

We’re prepared to put a competitive offer on the table: 4 years, averaging in the $18–19M AAV range. That reflects strong value for a player of his age and skill set while preserving our ability to add the necessary depth for a championship run.

If that range is workable, we can discuss structure and incentives. Let me know your thoughts.

Best regards,  
GM, Apex City Aces

**Agent:**

Kevin has a comprehensive conditioning and maintenance program that has significantly improved his availability. He's committed to being available for deep playoff runs and understands the demands of a contender. Given his elite scoring (9/10) and your secondary need at PF, he's looking for a 3-year deal at $12M AAV, which is well below his comparable Devon Miles ($15M AAV) due to his durability concerns.

**GM:**

**Subject: Re: Kevin Okafor**

Thank you for the detailed update. It’s encouraging to hear about Kevin’s commitment to his conditioning and availability—that’s essential for our playoff push.

While we value his scoring, a three-year term at that AAV introduces more long-term risk than we’re comfortable with, given our win-now mandate and cap planning. We’d be more interested in a shorter, high-value arrangement that aligns with our contention window.

We could consider a 2-year deal in the $10–11M AAV range, potentially with performance incentives tied to games played or postseason availability. This would offer Kevin a strong annual number while fitting our roster construction.

If a shorter term works, we can discuss specifics. Let me know.

Best regards,  
GM, Apex City Aces

Jaylen Brooks is a 22-year-old point guard with solid fundamentals and excellent durability. While his current production is modest, his age and potential fit perfectly with your rebuild timeline. He has upside to develop into a solid starter with the right development environment. Would you consider a longer-term investment?

**GM:**

**To:** Jaylen Brooks' Agent  
**From:** General Manager, Cascade Wolves  

Thanks for reaching out. Jaylen is exactly the type of young, durable guard we're looking to build with. His fundamentals and age align well with our timeline.

Before we talk numbers, I'd like to understand your view on his development path. What role do you see him growing into over the next few seasons, and how do you think our system could help him maximize his upside?

We're certainly open to a longer-term commitment for the right player, but we'd want to ensure the structure supports both his growth and our flexibility. Let me know your initial thoughts on term and annual value, and we can go from there.

Looking forward to the conversation.

**Agent:**

Jaylen has significant upside as a young point guard with excellent durability. We see him developing into a solid starter who can manage an offense efficiently while continuing to improve his scoring and playmaking. Your development system and playing time opportunities would be ideal for maximizing his potential.

Given Chris Yates' comparable contract (2yr/$6M) and Jaylen's similar profile, we're looking at 3 years at $4M AAV. This represents excellent value for a young, durable guard with upside in a rebuilding system.

**GM:**

**To:** Jaylen Brooks' Agent  
**From:** General Manager, Cascade Wolves  

Appreciate the clarity on his projected development path. We agree that Jaylen's durability and room for growth make him a strong fit for our rebuild.

While we see the value in a three-year commitment, the $4M AAV feels a bit elevated given his current production level and the fact that we're investing in upside, not established output. The Yates comparison is noted, but each situation has its own context.

Would you be open to a structure that starts lower in Year 1 with gradual increases, or a slightly lower AAV across the term? Something in the range of 3 years, $3–3.5M AAV would align better with our budget while still offering Jaylen security and a clear development runway here.

Let me know your thoughts.

**Agent:**

Jaylen's floor salary is $2M, so your range of $3-3.5M AAV is acceptable. Given his youth and upside, we believe $3.5M AAV represents fair value for a 3-year commitment. This is actually below the trajectory of similar young guards and provides excellent value for your rebuild.

Can we agree on 3 years at $3.5M AAV?

**GM:**

**To:** Jaylen Brooks' Agent  
**From:** General Manager, Cascade Wolves  

We can work with 3 years at $3.5M AAV. That structure gives Jaylen the security and runway he needs while keeping our investment aligned with his current development stage.

Given his age, durability, and fit with our timeline, we’re comfortable moving forward at those terms. I think we have a deal — send the close_deal call when you're ready to make it official and I’ll get the paperwork started.

**Agent:**

Marcus Cole is a 24-year-old elite scorer (9/10) with exceptional durability (9/10) who remains available in free agency. Given your rebuild philosophy and preference for young players under-25, he would be a perfect cornerstone for your future. His scoring ability and durability make him exactly the type of foundational piece you're looking to build around.

Would you consider a long-term investment in Marcus Cole?

**GM:**

**To:** Marcus Cole's Agent  
**From:** General Manager, Cascade Wolves  

Marcus is certainly an intriguing talent, and his age, scoring ability, and durability align with the profile we're targeting in this rebuild. He has the tools to grow into a cornerstone piece.

Before discussing numbers, I'd like to hear your perspective on his fit beyond just scoring. How do you see his game evolving in a system that prioritizes player development, and what role does he envision for himself as we build over the next few seasons?

We're open to a longer-term commitment for the right foundational player, but we'd want to ensure the structure supports both his growth and our roster-building flexibility. What are your initial thoughts on term and annual value?

Looking forward to your perspective.

**Agent:**

Marcus sees himself as a foundational piece who can grow into a franchise player. His game is built on efficient scoring through shot creation, cutting, and spot-up shooting. In a development-focused system like yours, he would have the opportunity to refine his off-ball movement and defensive skills while serving as your primary offensive weapon.

Given his elite scoring ability (9/10) and exceptional durability (9/10) at age 24, we're looking at 4 years at $22M AAV. This represents fair market value for a player of his caliber and provides you with a cornerstone to build around for your rebuild.

**GM:**

**To:** Marcus Cole's Agent  
**From:** General Manager, Cascade Wolves  

Thanks for outlining his vision and development path. We agree Marcus has the tools to grow into a primary offensive option and appreciate his focus on refining his off-ball and defensive game.

A four-year term aligns with our rebuild window, but $22M AAV is a significant investment for a player whose impact beyond scoring is still developing. While his scoring and durability are elite, we’re building a team, not just a roster, and need to balance cornerstone contracts with future flexibility.

Would you be open to a structure that starts lower in Year 1 with annual increases, or a slightly lower AAV across the term? Something in the range of 4 years, $18–20M AAV would better reflect both his current value and our budget constraints while still providing him long-term security and a central role here.

Let me know your thoughts.

**Agent:**

Marcus's floor salary is $18M, so your range of $18-20M AAV is acceptable. Given his elite scoring ability and your need for a foundational piece, we believe $20M AAV is fair for a 4-year commitment. This represents a $2M reduction from our initial ask while still reflecting his market value.

Can we agree on 4 years at $20M AAV?

**GM:**

**To:** Marcus Cole's Agent  
**From:** General Manager, Cascade Wolves  

We can work with 4 years at $20M AAV. That structure gives Marcus the long-term security and central role he’s looking for, while keeping our investment aligned with both his current impact and future growth potential.

Given his age, elite scoring, and durability, we’re comfortable moving forward at those terms. I think we have a deal — send the close_deal call when you're ready to make it official and I’ll get the paperwork started.
